<!--end
left
column-->












<div
class="right_col
col-a-2">













<div
class="header
artist_info_header
int-1
clearfix">














<h1
class="hed-1"
title="Bon
Jovi"
itemprop="name">Bon
Jovi</h1>














<div
class="header_btns">















<div
class="bookmark"
data-musicid="R82357"></div>














</div>













</div>













<div
class="int-1">














<div
class="content_right">















<div
class="artist_bio_container
clearfix">
















<div
class="artist_bio
short_bio">
















<div
class="artist_bio_inner">

















After
ushering
in
the
era
of
pop-metal
with
their
1986
blockbuster


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/slippery-when-wet-remastered"
class="hash">Slippery
When
Wet</a>
and
its
hit
singles
You
Give
Love
a
Bad
Name,
Wanted
Dead
or
Alive,
and
Living
on
a
Prayer,
Bon
Jovi
wound
up
transcending
the
big-haired
80s,
withstanding
changes
in
style
and
sound
to
become
one
of
the
biggest
American
rock
bands
of
their
time,
selling
over
120
million
albums
worldwide,
and
sustaining
their
popularity
well
into
the
new
millennium.
As
the
times
changed,
so
did
the
bands
sound.
They
slowly
peeled
away
the
arena
rock
guitars
of
the
80s,
occasionally
scoring
on
the
adult
contemporary
charts
and
sometimes
singing
country
music
without
ever
rejecting
hard
rock,
a
move
that
illustrated
how
they
never
abandoned
their
roots
and
became
second
only
to


















<a
href="/bruce-springsteen"
class="hash">Bruce
Springsteen</a>
in
defining
the
sound
and
spirit
of
New
Jersey
rock
&amp;
roll.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
Bon
Jovi
took
their
name
from
lead
singer


















<a
href="/jon-bon-jovi"
class="hash">Jon
Bon
Jovi</a>
(born
Jon
Bongiovi),
who
spent
his
adolescence
playing
in
local
Jersey
bands
with
David
Bryan
(born
David
Rashbaum).


















<a
href="/jon-bon-jovi"
class="hash">Jon</a>s
cousin,
Tony
Bongiovi,
owned
the
celebrated
New
York
recording
studio
the
Power
Station
and


















<a
href="/jon-bon-jovi"
class="hash">Jon</a>
spent
many
hours
there,
working
as
a
janitor
and
recording
demos
after
hours,
sometimes
supported
by
members
of
the
E
Street
Band
or


















<a
href="/aldo-nova"
class="hash">Aldo
Nova</a>.
One
of
those
demos,
&quot;Runaway,&quot;
became
a
hit
on
local
New
Jersey
radio
and
lead
to
the
formation
of
Bon
Jovi
the
band,
as


















<a
href="/jon-bon-jovi"
class="hash">Jon</a>
and
Bryan
were
supported
by
guitarist
Dave
Sabo,
bassist
Alec
John
Such,
and
drummer
Tico
Torres.
Runaway
spurred
a
major-label
bidding
war
leading
to
a
contract
with
Polygram/Mercury
in
1983.
Before
the
group
entered
the
studio,
though,
Bon
Jovi
replaced
Sabo
with


















<a
href="/richie-sambora"
class="hash">Richie
Sambora</a>,
a
working
guitarist
with
a
long
r&eacute;sum&eacute;
including
a
stint
as
a
member
of
Message.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
Bon
Jovi
released
their
eponymous
debut
album
in
1984,
generating
a
Top
40
hit
with
the
original
version
of
&quot;Runaway.&quot;
The
following
year,


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/7800-degrees-fahrenheit"
class="hash">7800&deg;
Fahrenheit</a>
was
released
and
went
gold,
all
serving
as
a
prelude
to
the
band's
1986
breakthrough,


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/slippery-when-wet-remastered"
class="hash">Slippery
When
Wet</a>.


















<a
href="/paul-stanley"
class="hash">Paul
Stanley</a>
had
given


















<a
href="/jon-bon-jovi"
class="hash">Jon</a>
and


















<a
href="/richie-sambora"
class="hash">Richie</a>
the
phone
number
of
professional
songwriter
Desmond
Child,
and
together
they
wrote
two
of
the
album's
biggest
hits
in


















<a
href="/richie-sambora"
class="hash">Richie</a>'s
parents'
basement.
The
trio
composed
30
songs
in
total
and
auditioned
them
for
local
New
Jersey
and
New
York
teenagers,
basing
the
album's
running
order
on
their
opinions.
Supported
by
several
appealing,
straightforward
videos
that
received
heavy
rotation
on
MTV,
the
record
took
off
on
the
strength
of
You
Give
Love
a
Bad
Name,
followed
quickly
by
Livin
on
a
Prayer
and
Wanted
Dead
or
Alive.
Those
three
Top
Ten
Hits
helped
propel


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/slippery-when-wet-remastered"
class="hash">Slippery
When
Wet</a>
to
sales
of
nine
million
in
the
U.S.
alone,
establishing
Bon
Jovi
as
superstars
in
their
home
country.
Their
fame
was
not
limited
to
the
U.S.,
though,
as
the
album
also
turned
into
a
significant
hit
in
Europe,
Canada,
Japan,
and
Australia.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
Bon
Jovi
built
upon


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/slippery-when-wet-remastered"
class="hash">Slippery
When
Wet</a>'s
formula
with
1988's


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/new-jersey"
class="hash">New
Jersey</a>,
which
shot
to
number
one
upon
its
release.


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/new-jersey"
class="hash">New
Jersey</a>
was
only
slightly
less
successful
than
its
predecessor,
selling
five
million
copies
and
generating
two
number
one
singles,
&quot;Bad
Medicine&quot;
and
&quot;I'll
Be
There
for
You,&quot;
as
well
as
the
Top
Ten
hits
&quot;Born
to
Be
My
Baby,&quot;
&quot;Lay
Your
Hands
on
Me,&quot;
and
&quot;Living
in
Sin.&quot;
Following
the
completion
of
an
18-month
international
tour,
the
band
went
on
hiatus.
During
the
time
off,


















<a
href="/jon-bon-jovi"
class="hash">Jon
Bon
Jovi</a>
wrote
the
soundtrack
for


















<i>Young
Guns
II</i>,
which
was
released
in
1990
as
the


















<a
href="/jon-bon-jovi/blaze-of-glory-young-guns-2"
class="hash">Blaze
of
Glory</a>
album.
The
record
produced
two
hit
singles
--
the
number
one
title
track
and
the
number
12
&quot;Miracle&quot;
--
and
earned
several
Grammy
and
Oscar
nominations.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
The
following
year,
Bon
Jovi
reunited
to
record
their
fifth
album,


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/keep-faith"
class="hash">Keep
the
Faith</a>,
which
was
released
in
the
fall
of
1992.
While
the
album
didn't
match
the
blockbuster
status
of
its
predecessors,
it
did
produce
a
hit
with
&quot;Bed
of
Roses,&quot;
an
adult
contemporary-styled
ballad
that
helped
sustain
the
bands
popularity.
A
greatest-hits
album
called
Cross
Road
appeared
in
1994
and
yielded
another
Top
Ten
ballad,
&quot;Always.&quot;
Around
the
same
time,
bassist
Alec
John
Such
left
the
band;
Hugh
McDonald,
who
appeared
on
Bon
Jovi
recordings
stretching
back
as
far
as
Runaway,
became
his
unofficial
replacement
and
featured
prominently
on
the
bands
next
album.
Released
in
the
fall
of
1995,


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/these-days"
class="hash">These
Days</a>
turned
into
another
U.S.
Top
Ten,
as
well
as
a
popular
European
hit.
After
appearing
in
the
1996
film


















<i>Moonlight
and
Valentino</i>,


















<a
href="/jon-bon-jovi"
class="hash">Jon
Bon
Jovi</a>
released
his
first
official
solo
album,


















<a
href="#"
class="hash">Destination
Anywhere</a>,
in
the
summer
of
1997.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
During
the
tail-end
of
the
'90s,
the
members
of
Bon
Jovi
engaged
in
different
projects
--


















<a
href="/richie-sambora"
class="hash">Sambora</a>
released
a
sophomore
solo
set
called


















<a
href="/richie-sambora/undiscovered-soul"
class="hash">Undiscovered
Soul</a>
in
1998
--
before
easing
back
into
work
in
1999
via
a
song
for
EdTV,
then
beginning
work
on
a
full-length
record.
The
resulting
album,


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/crush"
class="hash">Crush</a>,
appeared
in
2000
and
constituted
something
of
a
comeback
in
America
thanks
to
the
smash
single
Its
My
Life,
a
cross-platform
hit
single
with
long
legs.
Thank
You
for
Loving
Me
also
turned
into
a
hit,
helping


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/crush"
class="hash">Crush</a>
go
double
platinum
in
the
U.S.
and
selling
eight
million
copies
worldwide.
Bon
Jovi
quickly
followed


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/crush"
class="hash">Crush</a>
with
their
eighth
studio
effort,


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/bounce"
class="hash">Bounce</a>,
which
appeared
in
fall
2002,
and
supported
the
record
with
another
international
tour.
In
2003,
the
band
re-recorded
many
of
its
most
well-known
songs
for
the
acoustic-based
release


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/this-left-feels-right"
class="hash">This
Left
Feels
Right</a>,
which
also
saw
an
accompanying
DVD
in
2004.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
The
ambitious
outtakes
and
rarities
box
set


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/100000000-bon-jovi-fans-cant-be-wrong"
class="hash">100,000,000
Bon
Jovi
Fans
Can't
Be
Wrong</a>
arrived
later
that
November,
followed
by
the
all-new


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/have-nice-day"
class="hash">Have
a
Nice
Day</a>
--
the
first
of
several
albums
produced
by
John
Shanks.
That
album's
success
was
aided
in
part
by
the
single
Who
Says
You
Cant
Go
Home,
featuring
guest
vocals
from


















<a
href="/sugarland"
class="hash">Sugarland</a>'s


















<a
href="/jennifer-nettles"
class="hash">Jennifer
Nettles</a>,
which
eventually
won
the
Grammy
Award
for
Best
Country
Collaboration
with
Vocals
--
as
well
as
topping
the
charts
in
Japan,
Australia,
Europe,
and
Canada.
The
band
spent
the
following
year
in
the
studio,
putting
the
finishing
touches
on
a
collection
of
pop-infused
heartland
country
anthems.
The
resulting


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/lost-highway"
class="hash">Lost
Highway</a>,
which
featured
duets
with


















<a
href="/leann-rimes"
class="hash">LeAnn
Rimes</a>
and


















<a
href="/big-rich-country"
class="hash">Big
&amp;
Rich</a>,
arrived
in
the
summer
of
2007
and
grabbed
the
band
a
healthy
new
country
music
fan
base
in
the
process.


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/lost-highway"
class="hash">Lost
Highway</a>'s
cross-genre
formula
proved
to
be
quite
potent,
securing
the
band
its
third
number
one
album
in
the
U.S.
Bon
Jovi
returned
to
rock
shortly
thereafter,
though,
with
the
release
of
the
somber,
searching


















<a
href="/bon-jovi/circle"
class="hash">The
Circle</a>
in
2009.
One
year
later,
Greatest
Hits:
The
Ultimate
Collection
offered
plenty
of
hits
along
with
two
new
tracks,
No
Apologies
and
What
Do
You
Got?


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
In
the
first
years
of
the
2010s,
the
members
of
Bon
Jovi
pursued
solo
projects,
the
most
notable
being


















<a
href="/richie-sambora"
class="hash">Sambora</a>'s
2012
solo
album


















<a
href="/richie-sambora/aftermath-of-lowdown"
class="hash">Aftermath
of
the
Lowdown</a>.
Several
months
after
its
release,
Bon
Jovi
returned
with
What
About
Now,
their
first
album
in
four
years.
~
Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine,
Rovi
















</div>















</div>
















<a
href="#"
class="full_bio_link">full
bio</a>















</div>

One
Gift

to

One

(\"Purchaser\")

or
by

Pandora
One

and

(\"Recipient\").
The

in

Pandora
is

		<li>To

must

registration
information,
a
valid

at

purchasing
a
Pandora
One
Gift
Subscription,
you
authorize
Pandora
to
charge
the
purchase
price
of
the
Pandora
One
Gift
Subscription,
and
any
applicable

to
the

		<li>The
Purchaser
is

to

or
credit
for
any
reason,

without

if

Recipient

to

One

a

One

One
Gift

Pandora
One
Gift
Subscription

		<li>The
Purchaser
may
not
transfer
a

Pandora
One
Gift
Subscription
to

than
one
recipient.
A

One
Gift
Subscription
is
fully

by
the
Recipient
prior

or

In

Pandora
One

		<li>Recipients

One
